# Private Room — Feature Audit Summary (2026-07-18, re-verified against HEAD 5c16d71)

This file is the complete audit: this preface (TL;DR) followed by the full 1626-item catalog across 24 areas, every item with a `connected`/`partial`/`dead`/`planned` verdict and a file:line call-chain trace. Jump to [Table of contents](#table-of-contents).

**Searchable artifact:** https://claude.ai/code/artifact/89cf1668-0614-47e2-97eb-91f274336356 — filter by status/area/kind, full-text search across name/file/trace/notes.

**Method:** 22 agents each read one coherent slice of the codebase (frontend, Rust, Python sidecar) in full — not sampled — plus a roadmap agent cross-referencing the 13-idea backlog, followed by an adversarial re-verification pass on every "dead" claim against the whole repo. **Re-verified 2026-07-18** after 3 more commits landed (Wave 4a workflows-engine fixes + Wave 5 / Idea 13 room scripts): every prior dead-code finding was re-confirmed unchanged by direct grep, and the new Idea 13 feature got its own fresh full audit.

## Headline findings

1. **Idea 2 (LLM graph workflows + scheduler) was built live during this very audit.** Caught as an uncommitted, non-compiling stub; ~40 minutes later it was fully done — compiles clean, 20/20 tests pass, full frontend reachable from the Sidebar. Now committed.
2. **`sidecar/privateroom_sidecar/studios.py` is 100% dead code** — a fully-built, 24-test-covered module with a real HTTP route, but zero Rust callers. Re-confirmed still true at HEAD 5c16d71.
3. `file_pass.py`'s old `run_merge`/`run_compose` are dead legacy from before the sectioned-compose rewrite. Re-confirmed still true.
4. The agent's `mark_image` tool duplicates rather than reuses the sidecar's vision-grounding code.
5. `src/App.tsx` has a local `listRoles()` shadowing an identical, dead `api.ts` export.
6. **Idea 13 (runnable & schedulable room scripts) landed after the original audit and checks out clean** — a real `NodeKind::ScriptRun` integration into the Idea-2 workflow engine, SHA-256 consent gating, 21/21 script tests + full 316/316 suite passing. Surfaced two new partial findings: the generic agent/Leash `run_workflow` tool can silently re-trigger an already-approved script bypassing the Scripts UI, and deleting a scheduled script's file orphans its schedule with no cleanup surface.

## Stats

Of 1626 items catalogued: **1511 connected, 35 partial, 80 dead, 0 planned**.

## Methodology notes

- One of the 22 mapping agents returned a placeholder stub on the first pass despite passing schema validation — caught by spot-checking summaries, redone, and it surfaced the studios.py finding above. Schema validation guarantees shape, not content quality.
- This repo is under active, concurrent development — the Idea 2 workflows feature was built to completion *during* the audit's ~40-minute run, and Idea 13 landed in the time between the audit finishing and this "check again" pass. Treat any single-snapshot audit of this repo as perishable; re-check git status/cargo state before trusting it.

---

# Private Room — Full Feature & Connectivity Audit

_Generated by a 24-agent workflow (22 code-mapping agents covering every frontend, Rust, and Python sidecar file + 1 roadmap cross-reference agent + adversarial dead-code re-verification), followed by a dedicated live re-check of the Idea 2 / Workflows feature which was completed, compiled, and wired end-to-end **during the ~40 minutes this audit was running**. Branch `moonshot-impl`, base HEAD `9299081`, audit run 2026-07-18. **Re-verified 2026-07-18 at HEAD `5c16d71`** (3 commits later: Wave 4a workflows-engine adversarial-review fixes + Wave 5 / Idea 13 room scripts) — every prior dead-code finding re-confirmed unchanged by direct grep, and a dedicated fresh audit of the new Idea 13 feature was folded in below._

Every UI control, screen, end-to-end flow, Tauri command, and Python sidecar function is catalogued below with a `connected` / `partial` / `dead` / `planned` verdict and a concrete file:line call-chain trace. All `dead` verdicts were independently re-checked against the whole repository — either by a dedicated adversarial verifier agent, or (for the small batch of new dead-code findings surfaced by a targeted re-run late in the audit) by a direct manual grep spot-check.

## Headline findings

1. **Idea 2 (LLM graph workflows + scheduler) was built live during this very audit.** The mapping pass found `src-tauri/src/db/workflows.rs` as a brand-new, uncommitted, unwired file and the roadmap agent confirmed the crate didn't even compile. By the time the audit's final check ran ~40 minutes later, the feature was complete: a full frontend page (library, visual pipeline canvas, per-node parameter editor, scheduler popover, run history), a real DAG executor with branching, a tick-loop scheduler, 14 registered Tauri commands, 4 agent tool calls, Leash (external-MCP) exposure, and 20/20 passing tests. See [13-idea roadmap status](#13-idea-roadmap-status) and [Idea 2 / Wave 4a — Workflows feature](#idea-2--wave-4a--workflows-feature-built-live-during-this-audit-both-frontend-and-backend). **It is still uncommitted to git as of this report — recommend committing soon.**

2. **A duplicate, fully-built, fully-tested Python sidecar module is 100% dead code.** `sidecar/privateroom_sidecar/studios.py` (743 lines, 24 passing unit tests, wired into a real `POST /studio` FastAPI route) has **zero callers anywhere in the Rust or frontend code**. The live flashcards/mindmap/podcast studio feature runs through a completely separate native-Rust implementation (`src-tauri/src/commands/studios.rs::run_studio`) that talks to Ollama directly and never touches the sidecar. A source comment in `sidecar.rs:41` claims `studio` was migrated to the sidecar — that migration never actually happened in the Rust source. See the [Python sidecar: Heavy feature modules](#python-sidecar-heavy-feature-modules--file_pass-studios-summarize-vision) section.

3. **`file_pass.py`'s old merge/compose functions are dead legacy** from before the sectioned-compose rewrite (`run_merge`, `run_compose`, their request models, and the `/file_pass_merge`/`/file_pass_compose` routes) — confirmed zero callers repo-wide. The live path is the sectioned map → per-section compose → publish pipeline.

4. **The in-room agent's image-grounding tool duplicates, rather than reuses, the sidecar's vision code.** `vision.py`'s `vision_locate` only serves the manual "locate in image" UI action; the agent's own `mark_image` tool calls a fully duplicated native-Rust copy of the same prompt/schema/parsing logic in `commands/vision.rs`, bypassing the sidecar entirely.

5. One stale piece of dead code from the pre-integration period: `src/App.tsx` defines and calls a local `listRoles()` that duplicates an identically-named, fully-implemented `api.ts` export — the `api.ts` version has zero callers anywhere in the repo.

6. **Idea 13 (runnable & schedulable room scripts) also landed since the original audit, and checks out clean on a fresh audit** — a real integration into the Idea-2 workflow engine (`NodeKind::ScriptRun`), SHA-256 content-hash consent gating, 21/21 script tests + full 316/316 suite passing. It surfaced two new **partial** findings: the generic agent/Leash `run_workflow` tool can silently re-trigger an already-approved script bypassing the Scripts page (it cannot run unapproved/edited code), and deleting a scheduled script's file orphans its schedule with no cleanup UI. See [Idea 13 — Runnable & Schedulable Room Scripts](#idea-13--runnable--schedulable-room-scripts-landed-after-the-original-audit--verified-fresh).

**All 80 `dead` verdicts now carry independent adversarial-verification evidence** — 47 from the original audit's verify pass, plus 33 from a second, dedicated verify pass run after the user asked "all 80 dead confirmed?" (the studios.py cluster + file_pass legacy cluster had only been self-verified by the finding agent until then). Zero were refuted; zero came back uncertain.

### Idea 2 / Wave 4a — live update (read this first for Idea 2)

**Checked at the very end of the audit (2026-07-18, ~15 minutes after the 30-agent mapping workflow completed) — this section supersedes every earlier finding on this feature, including several `dead`/`planned` verdicts recorded elsewhere in this report before the feature finished landing.**

### Bottom line

**This feature went from "does not compile, 0% wired" to "end-to-end functional" during the ~40 minutes this audit was running.** A user can now open a real Workflows UI from the Sidebar, build a multi-node pipeline on a visual canvas, save it as a draft, activate it, run it manually, watch live per-node status during the run, inspect run history/artifacts, schedule it (interval/daily/weekly with catch-up), pin it to the top bar, and scope it to specific file types so it appears in a file's Actions menu. The in-room agent can list/draft/update/run workflows via 4 tool calls, and the external MCP bridge (the Leash) exposes the same 4 tools at the same trust tier as the file-pass job tools — confirmed never served to a cloud advisor by a passing regression test.

### Compile/test status — verified with a forced full rebuild, not a cached check

- `cargo check --lib` (after touching `lib.rs` to force a non-cached check): clean, 0 errors, 0 warnings.
- `cargo test --lib` on the workflow/scheduler surface: **20/20 pass** — `commands::jobs::scheduler::tests::*` (6/6, incl. DST-gap-day handling), `commands::jobs::workflow::tests::*` (8/8: validation, condition ops, edge liveness, compile/topo, run_input binding), `commands::agent::tests::{wants_job_tools_routes_workflow_intents, workflow_tools_never_leak_into_the_room_bridge_catalog}` (2/2), `db::workflows::tests::*` (3/3: CRUD/cascade, schedule upsert+due-read, migration on a pre-Wave-4a room).
- `npx tsc --noEmit`: zero errors across the whole TS tree, including all new `src/workspace/workflows/*.tsx` files.

The three compile blockers found by the roadmap agent ~40 minutes earlier are all confirmed fixed:
- **Missing scheduler module** → `src-tauri/src/commands/jobs/scheduler.rs` now exists, 259 lines, a complete tick loop (not a stub).
- **`run_via_sidecar` arg-count mismatch** → `sidecar.rs:317-338` added the `headless: bool` 10th parameter the workflow engine's caller expected; both call sites (visible-chat `agent.rs:802-811` passing `false`, headless workflow turn `jobs/workflow.rs:1076-1088` passing `true`) now match.
- **Async recursion type error in queue.rs** → resolved; the `pump`/`finish_and_pump`/`start_job_from_row` dispatcher chain now compiles.

### Backend — engine, scheduler, commands, agent tools, Leash

- **`src-tauri/src/commands/jobs/scheduler.rs`** (259 lines) — `next_run_after(kind, param, after)` computes interval/daily/weekly next-run times, DST-safe; `spawn_workflow_scheduler(app)` is generation-pinned (same pattern as the pre-existing embedding-backfill poller) and runs a 30s tick; `catch_up_pass` fires at most one catch-up per overdue schedule on unlock if opted in. Started from both `commands/rooms.rs:44` (create_room) and `:115` (open_room) — every room-open path starts the scheduler.
- **`src-tauri/src/lib.rs:226-240`** — 14 workflow-related `#[tauri::command]`s registered in `generate_handler!`: `save_workflow, update_workflow, delete_workflow, list_workflows, get_workflow, get_workflow_schedule, workflow_templates, run_workflow, set_workflow_schedule, set_workflow_status, set_workflow_pinned, validate_workflow, get_workflow_runs, get_job_step_artifact`.
- **`src-tauri/src/commands/jobs/workflow.rs`** (2108 lines) — `execute_workflow_step` (line 747) implements all 6 node kinds (`Generate`, `SummarizeFile`, `FilePass`, `AgentRun`, `SaveFile`, `Condition`) with real DAG dead-subgraph propagation (an unreached node is marked `skipped`, and that propagates transitively) — a real branching executor, not a linear runner. `run_agent_headless` (line 1050) pins to the room path (refuses if the room swapped underneath a scheduled run) and calls `run_via_sidecar(..., headless=true)` so scheduled/agent-driven runs never corrupt the visible chat stream. `spawn_workflow_job` (line 806) is a checkpointed runner persisting the full done-set per wave (needed for branched plans). `workflow_tools_specs()` (line 1829) returns the 4 agent-tool specs (`list_workflows`, `save_workflow`, `update_workflow`, `run_workflow`), each with a full worked-example JSON as a few-shot prompt.
- **`src-tauri/src/commands/jobs/queue.rs`** (341 lines) — single-slot FIFO queue (`pump`/`finish_and_pump`/`start_job_from_row`) aware of `parent_job_id` so a workflow's inline `file_pass` child job rides the parent's lane slot invisibly to independent pump/resume/quiesce; `resume_job` explicitly refuses inline children ("This job runs as part of a workflow — resume the workflow instead.").
- **`src-tauri/src/commands/agent.rs`** — `agent.rs:951-954` lists the 4 workflow tool names as agent-callable; `:1018` routes intent keywords (`workflow`, `automate`, `every morning`, `every day`, `every week`) toward job tools; `:2175-2181` `exec_tool` dispatches each to `agent_list_workflows`/`agent_save_workflow` (tags provenance `"agent"`)/`agent_update_workflow`/`agent_run_workflow`. Test-confirmed both present (`wants_job_tools_routes_workflow_intents`) and correctly scope-isolated (`workflow_tools_never_leak_into_the_room_bridge_catalog`).
- **`src-tauri/src/room_mcp.rs:482`** — `extras.extend(commands::workflow_tools_specs());` inside `scoped_specs`, gated behind `scope.include_job_tools()` (served to `LocalEngine`/`ExternalAgent`, never `CloudAdvisor` — enforced by a passing test at `room_mcp.rs:759-767`).
- **`src-tauri/src/db/schema.rs`** — `jobs.parent_job_id`, plus `workflows`/`workflow_runs`/`schedules` tables added to both the fresh-room `SCHEMA` constant and the guarded `migrate()` path (so existing rooms pick up the tables on open) — migration path is unit-tested and passing.
- **`src-tauri/src/db/workflows.rs`** (546 lines) — CRUD layer: `create_workflow/update_workflow/set_workflow_status/set_workflow_pinned/get_workflow/find_workflow/list_workflows/delete_workflow`, run tracking (`create_workflow_run/finish_workflow_run_by_job/list_workflow_runs`), schedules (`upsert_schedule/get_schedule/list_schedules/due_schedules/mark_schedule_run`).

### Frontend — a real page/canvas/library, reachable from the live UI

`src/workspace/workflows/` (7 files, 969 lines) is a complete feature module — see the dedicated "Frontend: Workflows feature" section of this report for the full per-component button/control breakdown (WorkflowsPage, WorkflowLibrary, WorkflowDetail, PipelineCanvas, NodeParamSheet, SchedulePopover, RunHistory). Reachability confirmed wired, not orphaned: a dedicated **Workflows** button in `Sidebar.tsx:119-127`; pinned workflows render as one-click TopBar shortcuts (`TopBar.tsx:44-98`, ⌘J popover) via the new generic `QuickActions.tsx` component; `state.ts:179-192` holds `showWorkflows`/`wfDetailId`/`workflows`/`wfNodeStatus` (live per-run per-node status); `ViewerPane.tsx:21,54-55` mounts `<WorkflowsPage/>` and also builds file-scoped quick-actions for the open file's Actions menu; `effects.ts` loads workflows on room open and subscribes to `onWorkflowNode`/`onWorkflowsChanged` live events; `api.ts:184-224` has a matching wrapper for every backend command plus the two event listeners; `apiTypes.ts:547-642` has full type parity.

### What's still open (nothing feature-blocking)

- `PipelineCanvas.tsx` uses deterministic auto-layout, not manual drag-and-drop — documented in its own code comment as a deliberate "v2" scope cut, not a bug.
- A cosmetic duplicated `#[allow(clippy::too_many_arguments)]` attribute line in `sidecar.rs` (harmless, doesn't affect compilation) — a sign the fix was done quickly, worth a quick cleanup pass.
- All of this is still **uncommitted to git** as of this check (`git status` shows it all as modified/untracked) — given how much has now landed and how cleanly it compiles and tests, this is worth committing soon.
- This report is based on full-tree compilation success (`cargo check --lib`, `cargo test --lib`, `tsc --noEmit`, all clean) plus direct reading of every relevant file — not on clicking through the running app, which was out of scope for this read-only pass.



### Idea 13 / Wave 5 — live update (read this first for Idea 13)

Landed in commit 2a470c5 ("Wave 5"), verified fresh at HEAD 5c16d71 (3 commits after the original audit snapshot). Turns any .py/.js file with a PEP-723-style manifest header into a runnable, schedulable script: uv run --no-project (or bare python3/node for dependency-free scripts) in a throwaway, 0700-permission, fully-scrubbed-env workspace; declared inputs materialized in, declared+new outputs imported back via the normal versioned store_file_bytes path. Implemented as a new NodeKind::ScriptRun on the Wave-4a workflow engine (every script gets a hidden auto-created single-node workflow), so scheduling/run-history/live-progress ride the existing queue/scheduler/workflow_runs tables -- not a parallel system. Consent is a per-Mac, SHA-256-content-addressed gate stored outside any .roomai file, with a data-agent-blocked first-run consent card; scheduled/agent runs re-hash at execution and hard-park on any mismatch. Health: 21/21 script-specific tests pass, full cargo test --lib 316/316 green, tsc clean, a real subprocess e2e test exercised actual python3. Does NOT touch the Python sidecar.

Two real gaps found on this fresh check: (1) the generic Idea-2 list_workflows/run_workflow tools (exposed to the in-room agent and to Leash LocalEngine/ExternalAgent scopes) are not filtered to hide a script's auto-created workflow, so an agent or external Leash client can silently re-trigger an already-approved script outside the Scripts page UI (it cannot run unapproved/edited code -- the hash re-check still hard-parks that). (2) deleting a scheduled script's file does not clean up its schedule/auto-workflow, which then fires and fails forever with no UI surface to see or cancel it.

## Frontend: Agent embodiment bridge + full API surface catalog

src/api.ts is the frontend's single gateway to all 128 Tauri commands; a repo-wide grep of every one of its ~144 exports found real call sites for the great majority, but surfaced a distinct cluster of 9 dead exports (recommendedModels, ensureEmbedModel, roomGraph, getOllamaUrl, setOllamaUrl, listRoles, writeRecoveryKey, openRoomWithRecovery, startFilePass) — each caused by the same pattern: a consuming file still carries a "CONTRACT-NOTE" explaining it was written in parallel before the api.ts wrapper landed and calls invoke() directly instead, so the wrapper was never folded in during integration. startFilePass is the most severe case: neither the JS wrapper nor its own Tauri command has any caller anywhere — the whole-file-pass feature is live only because the agent tool loop calls the underlying begin_file_pass() Rust helper directly, bypassing the registered command entirely. src/agent/driver.ts (the UI-driving agent↔webview bridge, ADD-25) is fully and precisely wired end-to-end: its four request kinds (ui_snapshot/ui_act/view_screenshot/media_frame) match the backend's request_ui() call sites exactly, it has exactly one frontend consumer (workspace/effects.ts, mounted from Workspace.tsx), and its selectors/consent-fence attributes all resolve against real, live DOM classes — with one small harmless issue (a stale `.top-bar`/`.viewer-pane` selector fragment that never matches, masked by a co-listed tag selector that still does). src/updater.ts, previously flagged in product notes as a "dead-updater gate," is now mechanically live end-to-end (plugin registered, capability-permissioned, real minisign pubkey + GitHub endpoint committed, matching git tags v0.1.0–v0.2.3 and a release.sh script exist) — it is best described as "partial" today only because its own source comments are stale (still claim the config is a placeholder) and this sandbox cannot verify the GitHub endpoint currently serves a resolvable latest.json.

## Frontend: Workspace chrome (TopBar, Sidebar, global overlays/modals/toasts, front page)

This area is the room's chrome shell around the file/chat panes: TopBar (room identity, engine/model pill, room menu, search, lock), Sidebar (file/folder tree, Add menu incl. recording entry points, background-job cards, memory panel), Overlays (capture dock, MCP/edit consent cards, file context menu, drag-drop, ⌘F search), plus the small satellite components (Toasts, SettingsModals/AddLinkModal, EngineModelPicker, DeleteControl, FeedbackModal, FileRow, FrontPage) and the rooms/ constants+helpers used by the pre-workspace screens. Every control traced resolves to a live handler in src/workspace/*.ts (fileActions/miscActions/recordingActions/studioActions/chatActions) that calls a registered api.ts→invoke()→#[tauri::command] wrapper, or is a pure client-side/OS-plugin action (client filter, Tauri opener, MediaRecorder) — I found no dead code in these 12 files: every export is imported and used by at least one live caller (Workspace.tsx, ComposerPane.tsx, ViewerPane.tsx, ChatPane.tsx, Settings/ModelSection.tsx, or the pre-workspace App.tsx/screens/*). The two data-agent-blocked consent surfaces this area owns (MCP tool-approval card, edit/diff-approval card) are confirmed enforced by a double fence in src/agent/driver.ts (excluded from ui_snapshot marks at snapshot time, re-checked at ui_act time) — the UI-driving agent genuinely cannot self-approve. The one piece of "being built right now" backend work (Wave 4a workflow jobs) touches none of these 12 files directly; Sidebar's job-card renderer is generic enough to already handle a future "workflow" job kind, but nothing yet creates one.

## Frontend: Workspace action/state dispatch layer

This layer (src/workspace/{actions,effects,fileActions,guard,miscActions,state,studioActions,types,constants}.ts) is the dispatch/reducer tier between the Workspace React tree and src/api.ts. useWorkspaceState holds ~90 state slots + refs; useWorkspaceActions composes 5 hook-factories (files/misc/recording/studio/chat/voice — only files/misc/studio are in this audit's file set) into one flat `a.*` object consumed by every pane component; useWorkspaceEffects owns the mount-time backend-event wiring and ~10 smaller orchestration effects. guard.ts is NOT an approval/consent gate — that's a naming mismatch in the task brief. guard.ts (runGuarded/tryToast/toastOllamaDown) is a generic async-action error-handling wrapper (busy-flag lifecycle + Ollama-down/stopped/plain-error taxonomy) used by nearly every action in fileActions/miscActions/studioActions/chatActions. The REAL agent-approval/consent gate is the `data-agent-blocked` DOM attribute (checked in src/agent/driver.ts's `handleAgentUiRequest`, wired into this layer only via effects.ts's onAgentUiRequest listener, ADD-25) — it is enforced entirely outside these 9 files, in Overlays.tsx/ViewerPane.tsx/DeleteControl.tsx/CompareModal.tsx/TopBar.tsx JSX and in src/agent/driver.ts. Overall the layer is heavily connected: of ~75 exported dispatch functions across fileActions/miscActions/studioActions, only 3 are dead — `submitLink` (miscActions.ts, superseded by AddLinkModal's own inline reimplementation), `clearPendingEditApprovals` (miscActions.ts, superseded by an inline duplicate in chatActions.ts), and `summarizeRoom` (studioActions.ts, superseded by the ADD-30 `startDeepSummary` background-job flow — its backing Rust command `summarize_room` and its `summarize-progress` event listener in effects.ts are consequently also unreachable in the live app). None of the 9 files reference the new, uncommitted Wave-4a workflow engine (db/workflows.rs) — confirmed via grep, zero references. None of these dispatch functions are called by the Rust agent tool loop (src-tauri/src/commands/agent.rs) or room_mcp.rs Leash directly — those are backend-only paths; the only way the autonomous agent reaches this layer is indirectly, by synthesizing DOM clicks through the ADD-25 UI-driving bridge (effects.ts:176-181), which is blocked from consent surfaces by data-agent-blocked.

So: a user or the agent can never actually create, edit, run, or schedule a workflow today — the scheduler will run forever finding zero due_schedules() rows in every real room. Marked 'partial' rather than 'planned' because, unlike typical PM-doc-only scaffolding, the full Tauri command surface is registered and would dispatch correctly if invoked, and the auto-start scheduler is live and running in every open room right now — it is one frontend PR away from being reachable, not a design doc. |

This matches the ideas-triage memory's framing of Idea 2 as one of the large (L) backlog items still in progress; it is further along than the memory's original 2026-07-18 triage suggested (memory predates the DB-layer work) but still has zero live entry points as of this audit. |

## Rust: Agent tool loop + edit tools (the core engine)

agent.rs is the tool catalog/dispatcher for the app's AI: it builds trust-tiered tool specs (base catalog, UI/perception, whole-file-pass, and Wave-1a ExternalAgent tools), and exec_tool is the single dispatcher every engine calls into. Since the "MIGRATION Phase 2b" cutover, the native Rust agent_loop is fully deleted — the Python/LangGraph sidecar is the sole local brain and reaches exec_tool only through the room_mcp loopback bridge (ToolScope::LocalEngine/CloudAdvisor/ExternalAgent), which agent_ui.rs's request_ui/resolve_agent_ui bridges out to the live webview (src/agent/driver.ts) for the four UI-driving tools. All four roadmap items for this wave are genuinely wired end-to-end: Idea 4 (fuzzy fallback + outcome telemetry) in edit_match.rs, Idea 7 (atomic multi-file edit_files) in edit_match.rs's plan_batch/commit_plans, Idea 6 (diff-preview approval gate, lock never held across the await) in edit_gate.rs with a real Overlays.tsx modal, and Idea 1 (ExternalAgent/"Leash full tier" + local_generate) wired through room_mcp.rs and commands/moonshot/server.rs with a live Settings toggle. The one significant regression found: the "AI advisors" (`consult_advisor`) feature has a fully live Settings toggle and persisted setting, but the tool spec is now never added to any catalog the sidecar or any bridge scope serves (advisors_on/advisor_tools_on are read then explicitly discarded as unused params in stream_answer, and the sidecar hard-codes `"advisors": []` and forbids the tool name defensively) — so toggling it on has zero effect today.

## Rust: Models, jobs engine, sidecar/Ollama lifecycle — INCLUDING the new in-progress workflows backend

Models/ollama/sidecar lifecycle and the ordinary jobs engine (deep-summary, whole-file pass, auto-index) are fully wired end-to-end from Settings/Sidebar UI and the agent tool loop — this part is healthy. The headline finding is about Wave 4a workflows: the task's briefed premise ("lib.rs has ZERO workflow references") is STALE — since that check, three new untracked files (commands/jobs/{queue,scheduler,workflow}.rs) were added that fully wire 14 workflow #[tauri::command]s into lib.rs's invoke_handler, plus a real queue/scheduler/DAG-executor. Four of those commands (list/save/update/run_workflow) are additionally reachable live today via the agent chat tool loop (and the Leash's ExternalAgent scope) — a user can already ask the agent to build and save a workflow in chat. But the whole feature is functionally a dead end at runtime: every workflow is created as 'draft' (hardcoded), db::set_workflow_status (the only draft→active flip) has ZERO callers anywhere — no UI, no agent tool — so no workflow can ever become 'active', which both agent_run_workflow and the (correctly wired, 30s-ticking) schedule tick loop require before running one. The DAG executor, node types, condition branching, file selectors, and the child-file_pass inline-job machinery are all fully built and unit-tested but have never executed outside tests. Zero frontend TypeScript exists for workflows (no page, no types, no event listeners for the emitted workflow-node/workflows-changed events) — the "Workflows page" the backend's own user-facing strings promise does not exist yet.

## Python sidecar: server wiring, config, routing, LLM/MCP clients

This slice is the sidecar's HTTP surface (26 FastAPI routes in server.py), its Pydantic contracts (config.py), deterministic tool routing ported verbatim from Rust (routing.py/prompts.py), the wire-message helpers (messages.py), the sidecar's own MCP client to the room "Leash" bridge (mcp_client.py), context-budget trimming (budget.py), two Phase-2 feature functions (features.py) and tool-step chip labels (labels.py). The great majority is genuinely wired end-to-end (confirmed via matching src-tauri/src/sidecar.rs and ollama.rs call sites): the core /run chat-agent loop, the LLM gateway (/embed, /generate, /generate_stream, /warm, /pull, /models, /delete, /capabilities), and most Phase-2 feature endpoints. Three routes are fully dead code with zero Rust callers (/studio — Rust's studios.rs calls Ollama directly instead; /file_pass_merge and /file_pass_compose — superseded by the sectioned-compose redesign but left in place), and several MCP-protocol methods (initialize/notify/ping, the async-context-manager dunders) are exercised only by tests, confirmed by test_integration.py's own comment that the real run path uses "exactly those two JSON-RPC methods (no initialize in-run)." Most notably, this session's supplied context ("lib.rs has ZERO 'workflow' references, nothing in workflows.rs reachable from any tauri::command") is stale as of current HEAD: routing.py/prompts.py were freshly edited to add four Wave-4a workflow tools to the agent's job-tool catalog, and direct greps show lib.rs registers 13 workflow tauri::commands (lib.rs:226-239) with full src/api.ts wrappers — but zero frontend component calls any of them, and no "Workflows page" exists anywhere in src/, so a workflow drafted via chat can never be activated and can never run.

## Python sidecar: Agent loop — chat, chat_docs, graph, LLM wrapper, AI actions

This is the sole AI engine for Private Room: graph.py's compiled LangGraph StateGraph (prepare -> call_model -> execute_tools -> synthesize) runs every local chat/agent turn, chat.py wraps ChatOllama for streaming + tool-calls, chat_docs.py and ai_actions.py serve narrowly-scoped Phase-2 feature endpoints (#extract/#add-file chat commands, the 14-action AiActionModal, memory suggestion, file-meta suggestion), and llm.py is the thin non-agent Ollama gateway (embed/generate/models) shared by all of them. Every function in all five files is reachable and exercised — I found zero dead code in this area. The one real finding: the roadmap's "sidecar permits exactly one retry" for failed edit-tool calls (graph.py:297-303) is not a hard cap — failed calls are simply never memoized in `seen`, so a model may retry an identical failing call in every subsequent round up to max_rounds (test_graph.py's "may retry" test only exercises one retry because that's what the scripted fake model does, not because the code enforces it). Separately, and outside this area's file scope but directly visible through graph.py's routing imports: the uncommitted Wave-4a workflow tools (list_workflows/save_workflow/update_workflow/run_workflow) are now fully wired end-to-end from the agent tool loop through Rust dispatch to the DB — contradicting the "lib.rs has zero workflow references" premise I was given — but they dead-end functionally because no frontend "Workflows page" exists to activate a draft, so `run_workflow` always errors today ("... is a draft — the user must activate it on the Workflows page").

| execute_tools: failed-call retry policy (the 'exactly one retry' claim) | python-fn | partial | sidecar/privateroom_sidecar/graph.py:277-303 | execute_tools loop (graph.py:277-303): 'key = call.key()' (name, canonical-JSON args, messages.py:55-57); 'if key in seen: skip as duplicate' (graph.py:283-286); tool runs (graph.py:291); 'if ok: seen.add(key)' ONLY on success (graph.py:297-299, comment: 'Only remember successful calls, so a failed one may retry once') | VERIFIED against the roadmap doc (pm-request/ideas-triage-2026-07-18.md:174, cites 'graph.py:297-299' — lines have NOT shifted, citation is accurate). But 'permits exactly one retry' overstates the guarantee: a FAILED call's key is never added to `seen`, so nothing blocks a 2nd, 3rd, ... Nth identical retry — it is bounded only by the round budget (PLAIN_MAX_ROUNDS=4 for a plain write-only turn per config.py:18/147-158, or MAX_TOOL_ROUNDS=1000 backstop otherwise per config.py:15) and the model's own willingness to keep repeating. sidecar/tests/test_graph.py:386-403 'test_a_failed_call_is_not_memoised_and_may_retry' only scripts ONE retry because that's what the fake chat model does, not because the code enforces a cap — the test name itself says 'may retry', not 'retries exactly once'. Net: the mechanism is 'unlimited retries permitted for failures' rather than 'exactly one retry granted.' |

The backend IS reachable today, including from the agent tool loop this area owns. What's actually missing is the FRONTEND: no page/component in src/ calls any Workflow api.ts wrapper (repo-wide grep confirmed, searched for listWorkflows\|getWorkflow\|saveWorkflow\|updateWorkflow\|deleteWorkflow\|runWorkflow\|workflowTemplates\|setWorkflowStatus\|setWorkflowPinned\|setWorkflowSchedule\|validateWorkflow\|getWorkflowRuns — zero hits outside src/api.ts). Net effect: an agent CAN save/list/update a workflow draft right now if a user's chat message contains a routing hint like 'automate' or 'every morning' (jobs routing fires -> the 4 workflow tools are offered), and list_workflows/save_workflow/update_workflow genuinely write to/read from the DB successfully — but run_workflow can never succeed (no path to 'active' status exists without the missing UI), and even a successfully-saved draft is permanently invisible to the user (no page renders it). This is exactly the 'being built right now' scaffolding the task asked me to represent precisely: backend + agent-loop wiring is real and live, the human-facing half of the feature is not. |
| seen (round-scoped set) / canonical_json duplicate-suppression key | python-fn | connected | sidecar/privateroom_sidecar/graph.py:117-118, 262, 282-286 | ToolCall.key() (sidecar/privateroom_sidecar/messages.py:55-57) returns (name, canonical_json(args)); execute_tools checks/updates the `seen` set each round | canonical_json sorts keys (messages.py:37-42) specifically so {"a":1,"b":2} and {"b":2,"a":1} count as the same call — verified by sidecar/tests/test_graph.py:368-384 'test_duplicate_key_ignores_argument_order'. |

## Python sidecar: Heavy feature modules — file_pass, studios, summarize, vision

Read all 4 files in full (2490 lines) plus server.py (530), sidecar.rs (~320 of 622 read), file_pass.rs (929), studios.rs (430), auto_index.rs (200+), jobs.rs/queue.rs/workflow.rs excerpts, vision.rs, summarize.rs, agent.rs excerpts, and src/api.ts. Headline findings: (1) file_pass.py's map/section path (the sectioned pipeline) is fully connected via THREE live entry points — the direct 'start_file_pass' command, the new (uncommitted but wired) Wave-4a workflow engine's file_pass node, and an agent MCP tool — but its merge/single-compose path (run_merge, run_compose, and the /file_pass_merge, /file_pass_compose endpoints) is DEAD: the Rust job DAG (file_pass.rs build_pass_steps) only ever emits 'map'/'compose'(sectioned)/'publish' steps, never a 'merge' step, and grep of all of src-tauri/src turns up zero callers of /file_pass_compose and zero non-test callers of /file_pass_merge — these are pure legacy leftovers from before the sectioned-compose rewrite (confirmed by the private-room-file-pass-sectioned memory). (2) studios.py's entire module — run_studio, all three _fallback_* renderers, all three render_*_html functions, the HTML templates, clean_studio_html, etc. — is 100% DEAD. It is fully built, unit-tested (sidecar/tests/test_studios.py, 24 tests), and wired into server.py's POST /studio route, but grep of the ENTIRE repo (src-tauri/src, src/, e2e/) found ZERO callers of '/studio'. The live studio feature (flashcards/mindmap/podcast) runs entirely through the OLD native Rust path in src-tauri/src/commands/studios.rs (run_studio) + studios/{flashcards,mindmap,podcast}.rs, which calls ollama::chat_structured directly and never touches the sidecar — the Phase-2/3 'MIGRATION' comment block that names 'studio' as a migrated feature (sidecar.rs:41) does not match the actual Rust source; studios.rs has zero MIGRATION/sidecar references. (3) summarize.py is fully connected — both summarize_one_file and combine_summary are reachable via TWO real entry points: the manual 'Summarize this room' button (summarize_room) and the durable, checkpointed 'deep_summary' job (start_deep_summary + auto-triggered via schedule_auto_index). Idea 8's stated gap ('hook file import to auto-enqueue deep_summary') HAS landed: auto_index.rs's schedule_auto_index is called at the end of import_files/run_ocr_job/run_stt_job and calls start_deep_summary_inner(auto=true) for large missing-summary drops. (4) vision.py's vision_locate is connected via ONE of two identical grounding features — the manual 'locate in image' UI action (ImageView.tsx -> locate_in_image command -> /vision_locate) — but the agent's own 'mark_image' tool (agent.rs) does NOT use it: it calls a fully duplicated native-Rust copy of prepare_image/grounding_prompt/boxes_schema/parse_boxes/boxes_from_items living in commands/vision.rs and talks to ollama::chat_structured directly, bypassing the sidecar entirely. So vision.py is connected but only serves half of the app's two vision-grounding call sites.

## Idea 2 / Wave 4a — Workflows feature (built live during this audit, both frontend and backend)

The entire LLM graph workflows + scheduler feature (Idea 2) — DB schema, executor, scheduler, agent tools, Leash exposure, and a full frontend page/canvas/library — was completed, made to compile, and wired end-to-end during the ~40 minutes this audit was running. It was 0% wired and failing to compile when the main 22-agent mapping pass read it; by the final check it was fully functional with 20/20 relevant Rust tests passing and a clean tsc. This section catalogues the finished feature; see the roadmap section's 'Idea 2 / Wave 4a — live update' for the narrative of what changed.

| Item | Kind | Status | File:Line | Trace | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|

## Idea 13 — Runnable & Schedulable Room Scripts (landed after the original audit — verified fresh)

Landed in commit 2a470c5 ("Wave 5"), on top of the Wave 4a workflows engine, unaffected by the later 5c16d71 fix commit. Turns any .py/.js file with a PEP-723-style manifest header into a runnable, schedulable script: `uv run --no-project` (or bare python3/node for dependency-free scripts) in a throwaway, permission-0700, fully-scrubbed-env workspace, with declared inputs materialized in and declared+new outputs imported back via the normal versioned store_file_bytes path. Implemented as a new NodeKind::ScriptRun on the Wave-4a workflow engine (every script gets a hidden auto-created single-node workflow), so scheduling/run-history/live-progress all ride the existing queue/scheduler/workflow_runs tables. Consent is a per-Mac, SHA-256-content-addressed gate stored outside any .roomai file, with a data-agent-blocked first-run consent card; scheduled/agent runs re-hash at execution and PARK on any mismatch. Health: 21/21 script-specific tests pass, full cargo test --lib 316/316 green, tsc clean, a real subprocess e2e test exercised actual python3. Does NOT touch the Python sidecar (no calls to /studio, /file_pass_merge, /file_pass_compose) — confirms those routes' dead verdict is unchanged.

| Python sidecar: Heavy feature modules — file_pass, studios, summarize, vision | run_studio | python-fn | sidecar/privateroom_sidecar/studios.py:575 | The live studio feature is 100% native Rust: commands/studios.rs run_studio (line 342) calls ollama::chat_structured directly (studios.rs:263,402), invoked by studio_flashcards/studio_mindmap/generate_podcast_script commands. This whole Python module — despite a docstring claiming it was 'ported' for the Phase-2 migration, being fully unit-tested (sidecar/tests/test_studios.py, 24 tests), and being wired into the FastAPI route table — has never actually been switched on from the Rust side. The sidecar.rs:41 comment listing 'studio' among migrated feature endpoints does not match the actual source. | Python sidecar: Agent loop — chat, chat_docs, graph, LLM wrapper, AI actions | execute_tools: failed-call retry policy (the 'exactly one retry' claim) | python-fn | sidecar/privateroom_sidecar/graph.py:277-303 | VERIFIED against the roadmap doc (pm-request/ideas-triage-2026-07-18.md:174, cites 'graph.py:297-299' — lines have NOT shifted, citation is accurate). But 'permits exactly one retry' overstates the guarantee: a FAILED call's key is never added to `seen`, so nothing blocks a 2nd, 3rd, ... Nth identical retry — it is bounded only by the round budget (PLAIN_MAX_ROUNDS=4 for a plain write-only turn per config.py:18/147-158, or MAX_TOOL_ROUNDS=1000 backstop otherwise per config.py:15) and the model's own willingness to keep repeating. sidecar/tests/test_graph.py:386-403 'test_a_failed_call_is_not_memoised_and_may_retry' only scripts ONE retry because that's what the fake chat model does, not because the code enforces a cap — the test name itself says 'may retry', not 'retries exactly once'. Net: the mechanism is 'unlimited retries permitted for failures' rather than 'exactly one retry granted.' |
| Python sidecar: Agent loop — chat, chat_docs, graph, LLM wrapper, AI actions | Wave 4a: workflow tools reachable via the agent tool loop (list_workflows/save_workflow/update_workflow/run_workflow) | flow | sidecar/privateroom_sidecar/graph.py:142-162 (via routing.py JOB_TOOL_NAMES, uncommitted diff) | IMPORTANT CORRECTION to the task's premise: I was told 'lib.rs has ZERO workflow references anywhere, meaning nothing in workflows.rs is reachable from any #[tauri::command] yet' — that is FALSE as of the current working tree. git diff src-tauri/src/lib.rs shows 15 newly-added lines registering commands::save_workflow/update_workflow/delete_workflow/list_workflows/get_workflow/get_workflow_schedule/workflow_templates/run_workflow/set_workflow_schedule/set_workflow_status/set_workflow_pinned/validate_workflow/get_workflow_runs/get_job_step_artifact in the invoke_handler (lib.rs, 'Wave 4a (Idea 2)' comment). The backend IS reachable today, including from the agent tool loop this area owns. What's actually missing is the FRONTEND: no page/component in src/ calls any Workflow api.ts wrapper (repo-wide grep confirmed, searched for listWorkflows\|getWorkflow\|saveWorkflow\|updateWorkflow\|deleteWorkflow\|runWorkflow\|workflowTemplates\|setWorkflowStatus\|setWorkflowPinned\|setWorkflowSchedule\|validateWorkflow\|getWorkflowRuns — zero hits outside src/api.ts). Net effect: an agent CAN save/list/update a workflow draft right now if a user's chat message contains a routing hint like 'automate' or 'every morning' (jobs routing fires -> the 4 workflow tools are offered), and list_workflows/save_workflow/update_workflow genuinely write to/read from the DB successfully — but run_workflow can never succeed (no path to 'active' status exists without the missing UI), and even a successfully-saved draft is permanently invisible to the user (no page renders it). This is exactly the 'being built right now' scaffolding the task asked me to represent precisely: backend + agent-loop wiring is real and live, the human-facing half of the feature is not. |

| Idea 13 — Runnable & Schedulable Room Scripts (landed after the original audit — verified fresh) | get_script_manifest (tauri command) | tauri-command | src-tauri/src/commands/scripts.rs:249-254 | A reasonable general-purpose API surface mirroring the workflow pattern, just not yet consumed by any component. |
| Idea 13 — Runnable & Schedulable Room Scripts (landed after the original audit — verified fresh) | Agent/Leash indirect script trigger via generic run_workflow | flow | src-tauri/src/commands/jobs/workflow.rs:1833-1871, 1971-1996 | Real live gap: an in-room agent or external Leash client at LocalEngine/ExternalAgent tier can discover an already-approved script's auto-workflow by name via list_workflows and silently re-trigger it via run_workflow with no fresh consent card and no Scripts-page visibility of the trigger. It CANNOT run unapproved/edited code -- the executor still re-hashes and hard-parks on any mismatch -- but it bypasses the intended 'always goes through the Scripts UI' assumption. The created_by=='script' filter that hides these rows exists only on the frontend (WorkflowLibrary.tsx diff lines 30-36), not in db::list_workflows or the agent/Leash tool layer. |
| Idea 13 — Runnable & Schedulable Room Scripts (landed after the original audit — verified fresh) | Orphaned schedule on script file deletion | flow | src-tauri/src/commands/files.rs:414-433 (delete_file) | A scheduled script whose file is deleted keeps firing (and failing cleanly) indefinitely on the scheduler's tick, invisible on both the Scripts page (file-driven listing, so the deleted file simply vanishes from it) and the Workflow Library (frontend hides created_by=='script' rows). No UI surface exists to see or cancel the orphaned schedule. This is an absence, not a broken call site -- the fix doesn't exist yet. |
